# DECISIONS LOG — "The Civil War" autonomous build run

Per Aaron's locked operating parameters (run i, 2026-06-13): **run the whole arc · always decide & log · auto-commit AND push at gated milestones · content-complete each phase.** Every design fork I resolve mid-run is recorded here with rationale so Aaron can override in review. Aaron-locked decisions (via popup) are marked **[AARON]**; ones I made under "always decide & log" are **[CLAUDE]**.

Format: `Dn · [who] · phase · decision — rationale (reversible? / impact)`

---

## Run-i operating parameters — [AARON] (popup, 2026-06-13)
- **D0a** Run scope = **run the whole arc** (S0→S5 then tactical), stop only at an unresolvable fork / unfixable gate failure / done; auto-handoff at context pressure.
- **D0b** Fork policy = **always decide & log** (never pause mid-run; this file is the log).
- **D0c** Commits = **auto-commit AND push** at each gated milestone (clear message + RUN-LOG entry).
- **D0d** Content = **content-complete each phase** (real citation-grade data + PD images per system; slower per phase, less rework). NOTE: the S0 cabinet is the one explicit exception — Aaron chose engravings-now / PD-photos-in-S2 in the same popup round (D4); the content-complete policy governs S1 onward.

## S0 — President's-Desk shell + build system
- **D1 · [AARON]** Build system = **frozen `build/base.html` (byte copy of the run-h monolith) + ordered `src/*.js` modules + zero-dep `tools/build.mjs`** that concatenates + splices before the unique engine-end anchor and re-emits `civil_war_generals.html`, gated in-memory (parse/hex/collision) before writing. — Honors the handoff's "modularize via a zero-dep concat build step, keep the current HTML as the base." Classic stays frozen (base never edited). (Reversible.)
- **D2 · [AARON]** Desk structure = **expand the War Department in place** — `openWarDept` redeclared to render the President's Desk; its 1864 Clock / Muster Roll / War Room become tabs alongside new The-War-Effort / Cabinet / Theater-Map tabs. One owner-mode screen, no parallel system (§1/§11). (Reversible.)
- **D3 · [AARON]** Strategic-turn surface = **auto-surface, one-click skip** — a "To the Executive Mansion" interstitial between battles (wraps `openUpgrade`); Continue proceeds to the Quartermaster, or open the desk. (Reversible.)
- **D4 · [AARON]** Cabinet (S0) = **stub now with procedural engraved portraits** (4 named secretaries per side); real advisor auto-manage/teach (R25) + PD photos in S2. (Reversible.)
- **D5 · [CLAUDE]** Main-menu button relabel **DEFERRED to S1** — `openMainMenu` is a 124-line broadsheet builder; redeclaring it to rename one cosmetic button (`#gnWarDept` → "The President's Desk") is the highest-churn override in S0 for a purely visual gain. The existing button already opens the (now-expanded) desk; the desk is also reachable from the interstitial. — Risk/benefit. (Reversible; do in S1 once stable.)
- **D6 · [CLAUDE]** Keep the generated `civil_war_generals.html` **committed** (not gitignored) — the deliverable premise is open-and-play from a fresh clone with no build step for the player; the build is a developer tool. `build/base.html` is the source of truth for the frozen foundation. (Reversible.)
- **D7 · [CLAUDE]** **No `_SAVE_VER` bump** for S0 — new `G.campaign.president` is additive plain data that rides `serializeSave` automatically; back-compat = idempotent `presInit` (lazy migration on next desk-open or battle-resolve). Bumping the version would silently erase every existing ver-1 save. (Reversible only forward.)
- **D8 · [CLAUDE]** Strategic-date cadence = **~1 month per battle placeholder**, synced up to the 1864 Clock's year. — S0 is a shell; real variable pacing (weekly in season, compressed in winter, §22) lands with the strategic-turn-loop content in S1. (Reversible.)

## S1 — economy (content-complete from research)
- **D9 · [CLAUDE]** Economy content gathered via a **citation-grade research workflow** (8 agents) → `HISTORICAL-DATA-ECONOMY.md` (digest + 28 debate cards) + `data/economy.json` (game-ready params). — Honors "content-complete each phase." (Source of truth on disk.)
- **D10 · [CLAUDE]** Build is now **data-driven**: `tools/build.mjs` injects `data/*.json` as a `GAME_DATA` global so `data/economy.json` is the single source of truth while the deliverable stays single-file. — Cleaner than inlining params in modules; sets up all of S1. (Reversible.)
- **D11 · [CLAUDE]** S1a = **the finance core first** (the spine + the most teachable system): three funding levers (bonds/taxes/printing), an EMERGENT inflation model (thin CS bond absorption + ~0.10 tax efficiency force the printing press → compounding spiral; US bonds+taxes cover demand → anchored), inflation→`clock.weariness` interlink. Production/cotton-blockade/manpower are S1b–S1d. — The asymmetry must be emergent from real params, not scripted (R29). (Reversible.)
- **D12 · [CLAUDE]** Treasury is **delegated to the Secretary by default** (auto-managed historical mix), opt-in to self-manage (balance principle §27). New "The Treasury" tab (7th desk tab). (Reversible.)
- **D14 · [CLAUDE]** S1b production layer **EXTENDS the War Room** (reads `wr.nodes` as inputs; does NOT redeclare wr → zero regression risk) rather than a parallel system. Asymmetric matériel: US well-found; CS throttled by iron ceiling + import-dependence + IRREVERSIBLE rail decay (~7%/turn) → ragged/hungry armies, emergent. Surfaced in the War Effort overview (no new tab). Probe-verified: US rail100/equip100/arms85 vs CS rail42/equip24/arms4/food19%. (Reversible.)
- **D15 · [CLAUDE]** Local commits only, **no GitHub push** — Aaron confirmed (run i): "just use local commit, should be fine not pushing to github." Supersedes the D0c push intent. (Reversible.)
- **D13 · [CLAUDE]** Inflation **calibration**: per-turn `_ecDEMAND=100`, US `inflCoeff≈0.06`/cap 4%, CS `inflCoeff≈0.18`×`spiralCoefficient^hiPrintTurns`. Probe-verified over 12 turns: US ×1.13, CS ×87.5 (≈ historical ~90× target), ratio 1:77. These are calibration starts per `economy.json` designerGaps — playtest to tune; turnCount still unset (rates documented for a 16-turn war). (Reversible.)

## S1c — cotton / blockade / foreign recognition
- **D16 · [CLAUDE]** S1c **EXTENDS, does not redeclare**: new `src/60-blockade.js` + `G.campaign.blockade` (sibling state); the production `importFactor` placeholder is wired by EDITING the `prodOnResolve` body (a src module I own, not the frozen base) to read `C.blockade.importFactor` with the static `cfg.importFactor` as fallback — no new manifest override. `blockadeOnResolve` registered in the existing `_t1Resolve` override BEFORE `prodOnResolve` so the fresh importFactor gates CS arms the same turn. — Lowest-regression wiring; zero new overrides. Probe-confirmed off>full arms. (Reversible.)
- **D17 · [CLAUDE]** The 1861 cotton **self-embargo is ON by default for CS** (historical: planters/committees drove it) and **auto-expires at year≥1862** (Richmond's hunger for hard currency overrode coercion). Player can lift it early via the Diplomacy tab. Recognition gained while the embargo is active = 0 (the trap: coercion against a glutted Britain bought nothing). — Models the self-sabotage as a *tempting* lever that quietly bleeds the treasury (per the `cotton-self-embargo` card takeaway), not a scripted penalty. (Reversible.)
- **D18 · [CLAUDE]** Foreign recognition is **foreclosed at year≥1863** (decay 0.5, boosts→0), with a 1862 window where it rises (Lancashire famine + early CS wins) then collapses. The S1c numbersAudit endorsed exactly this ("model a recognition window that narrows sharply after Sep 1862 and effectively closes by spring 1863," not a hard Proclamation cutoff). Recognition pulls `clock.intervention` toward itself (×0.30/turn) so even CS battlefield wins can't conjure intervention. — Honest contingency: the one real window, then the door shuts. (Reversible.)
- **D19 · [CLAUDE]** **Erlanger correction applied to `data/economy.json`**: `netProceedsPct` 0.72 → **0.45**, added `issuePriceToErlanger:77` / `publicOfferPrice:90`. The S1c numbersAudit (Gentry 1970) found 77 was Erlanger's BUY price (90 the public offer), and after the post-Vicksburg/Gettysburg slide + Confederate price-propping repurchases the net realized was ~£1.4M of £3M (~45%, not 72%). The Erlanger LEVER itself is deferred to S1d/S2 finance; the corrected figure is on disk for when it's built. Audit also flagged the `cottonBlockade.aggregateExportThroughputVsPeacetime: 0.11` as muddled (true blockade-run cotton to Europe ~3-4% of normal), but the sim doesn't read that field — the revenue-collapse curve (129→53) carries the teaching point; flagged for playtest, not changed. (Reversible.)
- **D20 · [CLAUDE]** **Citation-grade content via an 11-agent workflow** (5 research → 5 adversarial-verify → 1 numbers-audit) → `data/diplomacy.json` (multi-voice cards: consensus + scholarly dissent + named-and-countered Lost Cause + primary sources, Verified/Inferred provenance) + `HISTORICAL-DATA-DIPLOMACY.md`. The Verify pass removed 3 fabricated/misattributed citations (e.g., Egnal's *Clash of Extremes* mis-cited; a fabricated "Weidenmier & Brown" co-author). — Honors content-complete + the adversarial-verify quality bar. (Source of truth on disk.)

## S1d — manpower / conscription (the war-ender)
- **D21 · [CLAUDE]** S1d EXTENDS: new `src/70-manpower.js` + `G.campaign.manpower` (sibling); `manpowerOnResolve` registered in `_t1Resolve` AFTER prod (reads `B.casualties[side]` + the year). No new manifest overrides. **`C.manpower.strength` (0-100) is the army-strength index the S5 pre-battle bridge will read** — S1d produces the strength number that conditions battles. (Reversible.)
- **D22 · [CLAUDE]** The **replacement-ratio collapse is the war-ender**, modeled as the decisive asymmetry: US holds 1.0 (deep refillable pool); CS falls **0.9→0.6(1863)→0.3(1864)→0.1(1865)** by year. The S1d numbersAudit marked the precise ratios DISPUTED ("DIRECTION confirmed; precise ratios not a published statistic") — so they stay **calibrated designer values** (economy.json `replacementRatio._inferred:true`), directionally correct. Probe-verified: CS strength 99→53 (melting), pool→0 by 1865; US strength holds 100. (Reversible — playtest to tune.)
- **D23 · [CLAUDE]** Mechanics from the verified data: **Union draft = a coercive STIMULUS** (×1.2 volunteer inflow at 1863), NOT a direct manpower add — only ~6% of Union soldiers were direct draftees (Geary; audit CONFIRMED); **CS draft load-bearing** (1862, a year earlier); **USCT one-time +180k pool at 1863** (a new pool from the South's labor base); **immigrant inflow US-only** (~25% foreign-born). CS age-band widens 18-35→17-50 (1864) as a visible crisis 'tell'. Surfaced as a **"The Ranks" overview block** in the War Effort tab (NOT a 9th desk tab — tab economy; pairs with the production block), delegated to the Sec. of War, ambient teaching line (R26). (Reversible.)
## S1e — Paths to Victory (the South can win; performance, not script) — [AARON directive]
- **D25 · [AARON]** **The asymmetric collapse must be EMERGENT, not scripted.** Aaron caught that S1c/S1d keyed the Confederate death spiral to the calendar (ratio by year, recognition foreclosed 1863, ports fall on schedule), making defeat feel inevitable — contra §5 (deterministic by performance), §8 (the South wins by not losing), §29 (fair sandbox). FIX: `src/80-victory.js` adds `vicMomentum(C)` (a 0..1 war-fortunes signal from win-rate/will/capital); blockade + manpower now read it. **Winning → desertion ~0, ranks refill, ports hold, recognition stays open.** History is only the default-if-losing. Probe-verified (winning South: str 93/desert 9/ratio 0.83/ports held; losing: str 38/desert 297/ratio 0.22/foreclosed). (Reversible — but this is the locked design intent.)
- **D26 · [CLAUDE]** The replacement-ratio year curve became a "if losing" FLOOR (raised 1865 floor 0.1→0.18 so a passive South isn't instant-doomed) that momentum lifts toward 0.95; desertion = `(1-momentum)^1.6 * 16`. New `C.strategy.enemyWill` (the opponent's resolve) — winning erodes it → at ≤30 (1864+) the **negotiated-peace victory** becomes reachable (`victoryReady`). The S5 win-screen reads this. (Reversible.)
- **D27 · [CLAUDE]** **Executable Southern counter-levers** (new "Paths to Victory" 9th desk tab, side-aware): invest in blockade-runners (+importFactor), commission commerce raiders, fortify ports (hold past historical fall), pursue recognition (keep window open), deserter amnesty, arm-and-free the enslaved (Cleburne, +600 pool +0.3 ratio floor, one-time legitimacy shock). The US gets a mirror (Conquer / Hold Political Will / Strangle by Blockade). — Gives the player real avenues to execute each path (Aaron). (Reversible.)
- **D28 · [AARON]** **Wild-card catalog — alt-history gambits for BOTH sides, tiered plausible→long-shot→fantastical/preposterous** (Aaron: "creative and absurd to preposterous okay if I'm entertained… this is a game"). 11 CS (Trent crisis, invade North, burn-cotton, Cleburne, repeater smuggling, Northwest Conspiracy, Hunley fleet, Maximilian's legions, Stonewall-lives, **the Decapitation Plot** [momentum-gated: lands or backfires], Arizona gold) + 10 US (Hard War, radical 1861 emancipation, Anaconda overdrive, repeater army, Grant-early, greenback firehose, Gatling legions, Russian alliance, rail artillery, the general strike of the enslaved). Each one-shot, effect in `_vicApplyWild`. (Reversible; expandable.)
- **D29 · [CLAUDE]** probe-manpower/probe-blockade reframed to drive a LOSING South (the historical-default trajectory) for their collapse assertions; the WINNING-escapes case is proven by the new `tools/probe-victory.mjs` (12/12). (Test-only.)

## S1d — manpower / conscription (the war-ender)

Verify pass removed a misattribution (Fry's Final Report is a standalone 1866 doc, not OR Series III). **Unlike S1c, no sim data correction was required.** (Source of truth on disk.)

- **D30.16** Conflicting on-disk numbers ⇒ auto-correct to better-sourced value + log citation (Erlanger pattern).
- **D30.17** Player voice = period-flavored but tight; depth opt-in.

- **D30.20 ⚑** Onboarding = build a FULL guided tutorial — Aaron chose full over the recommended light/skippable (keep it skippable for experts regardless).

## D42 — A1 CANNON CORPS: hardening + the CS artillery asymmetry made mechanical — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
Finishing the scaffolded A1 Cannon Corps. An adversarial bug-hunt workflow (5 lenses × independent verify, 21 agents) confirmed **9 real findings** (7 correctly refuted as unreachable/cosmetic); all 9 fixed in `src/56-artillery.js` + `data/artillery.json`.
- **D42.1 (save integrity)** `artInit` now guards arrays explicitly (`Array.isArray`) at BOTH the `C.artillery` and `.batteries` levels — `typeof [] === "object"` let a corrupt/imported array survive, and a JSON round-trip serializes an array as `[]` and drops every named property → the whole park silently wiped on the next save. Battery COUNTS are now coerced/sanitized at the same chokepoint (`"3"`→3; drop null/NaN/objects/≤0).
- **D42.2 (the balance bug)** the 4-vs-6 guns-per-battery handicap was **purely cosmetic** (shown in the UI, zero mechanical effect — CS and US scored identically). `artBatteryScore` now scales coverage by the side's gun ratio (CS 4/6 ≈ 0.667), so a CS battery fills the park ~2/3 as fast; the South needs ~18 batteries to match a full Union park.
- **D42.3 (CS stacking penalties — designer calibration, Inferred)** the STRATEGIC pre-battle score now also models, CS-only: fuze unreliability ×0.96 (expected-value haircut for shell/case duds; solid shot & canister immune), horse/forage mobility ×0.95 from 1862 / ×0.88 from 1864, mixed-caliber resupply ×0.94 at 3+ calibers; plus the **1863 massing reform** as a both-sides bonus (US ×1.08 / CS ×1.04 — the Union's larger factor stands in for the army-level Artillery Reserve the ANV abolished after Chancellorsville). The per-shot fuze roll, the Whitworth ammunition cap, and gun-loss-on-retreat are **DEFERRED to the battle-day layer (A6) / tactical engine (P-phases)** where they belong as live rolls, not score haircuts. `_designNote` updated to record implemented-vs-deferred.
- **D42.4 (Whitworth import)** the rare British import now costs BOTH sides a premium (CS ×1.5 blockade / US ×1.2 foreign-import) instead of the Union buying the catalog's best gun at base price; `csOnly` kept false (both sides fielded a handful).
- **D42.5 (hardening)** `_artCost` honors a configured cost of 0; no-`id` guns are skipped in scoring + refused at purchase; `_artEsc` escapes data fields before `innerHTML`; `artBuy` coerces `n` via `Number()`; the baseline is clamped into [0,100]. *(The parallel unescaped-data gap in `55-weapons.js` is the same latent, non-triggering issue — flagged as a follow-up hardening item, not fixed in this A1-scoped commit.)*
- **Verified:** probe-cannon now **9/9** (added a US>CS divergence assertion that also asserts CS isn't crushed to baseline — accessible default per D35/§8.15); full no-regression suite green (diag-classic Classic paints, desk 12/0, weapons 8/0, bridge 6/0); 0 pageerrors. Sample (1863, 6× howitzer12 Q58): **US 44 vs CS 33**; bridge artillery facet 8→63 lifts overall 76→83.

## D43 — A2 ENGINEERING WORKS CORPS: buildable engineer arm + the rail-repair-that-can't-rebuild — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The Engineering Works Corps — the third buildable in The Armory (after small arms + the Cannon Corps). Four capabilities raised in levels 0-3 with funds: Construction Corps (Haupt's USMRR rail/bridge repair), Field Fortifications (the spade), Pontoon Train (river crossings), Siege Works (saps/parallels). New `src/57-engineering.js` + `data/engineering.json` + `C.engineering`. Feeds the battle bridge as an additive `engineering` facet (weight 0.10); construction raises the supply facet, pontoons lower fatigue; the Construction Corps claws back a FRACTION of each turn's rail loss (slows but never stops the CS rail collapse). CS pays a 1.25× materials premium — Union engineering vastly outstripped the South's (the USMRR rebuilt faster than the CS could wreck).
- **Content:** an 8-agent research+verify workflow → **4 Verified multi-voice teaching cards** (Haupt/USMRR; the spade & fieldworks; pontoon mobility; siege engineering). Anti-Lost-Cause: Solonick's "Vicksburg was dug out, not starved out"; the rifle-musket-vs-entrenchment debate surfaced (Griffith vs Hess); the Cold Harbor "7,000 in minutes" myth corrected (Rhea, ~6,000 Union for the day); Vauban dated correctly (17th c.). Every citation independently fact-checked; the verify pass fixed real errors (rank anachronisms, Petersburg mileage, the Foote attribution).
- **Mechanics (designer calibration, Inferred):** baseline 12; scorePerLevel construction 8 / fortifications 7 / pontoons 6 / siege 7 (full park ≈ 96); construction supply +4/level; pontoons fatigue −3/level; costPremiumCS 1.25.
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × independent verify, 19 agents) → **5 confirmed findings, all fixed** (9 correctly refuted as dev-console-only / intended-design):
  - **D43.1 (the real one)** the rail-repair was a CONSTANT additive (`level × 1.6`) against MULTIPLICATIVE decay → a stable equilibrium, and with the rail War-Room node funded it **pinned rail at 100 forever** (and recovered net-positive from a low point) — flatly contradicting the locked "irreversible decay, still declines" intent. **Fix:** `prodOnResolve` now stashes `railLossLast`; `engOnResolve` claws back only `min(0.70, 0.24×level)` of that loss (a sub-1.0 fraction), so the net trend is strictly negative for every decay/level/node combination. Probe asserts rail never pins at 100 and declines monotonically with the rail node maxed (verified: 100→84 with full construction, vs 55 without).
  - **D43.2** `perLevelEffect`/`scorePerLevel` lacked NaN/negative guards (a data typo could NaN or *invert* supply/fatigue) → Number/isFinite/floor-guarded; a configured `scorePerLevel` of 0 is now honored.
  - **D43.3** boolean-in-save coerced to level 1 (`Number(true)===1` → a free capability) → `engInit` rejects non-number/string before coercion. **Parity fix applied to `artInit` (A1) too.**
  - **D43.4** `_engEsc` didn't escape quotes but `b.id` sits in a `data-engbuy="…"` attribute → quote-escaping added. **Parity fix to `_artEsc` + the `data-artbuy` attribute (A1) too.**
  - **D43.5** a bare `&` in static render text → `&amp;`.
- **Verified:** probe-engineering **9/9** (incl. the new equilibrium-regression assertion); full no-regression green (diag-classic Classic paints; production/cannon/bridge/desk unaffected — the prod `railLossLast` + artillery parity edits caused no regression); 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈947KB.

## D44 — A3 TERRAIN COVER HIERARCHY: the first frozen-engine override — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The first frozen-engine override under §8.2. Six named cover types (Stone Wall, Entrenchments, Sunken Road, Boulders, Dense Forest, Rail Fence) slotted into the engine's EXISTING terrain/defense model. New `src/58-terrain-cover.js` + `data/terrain-cover.json`.
- **Mechanism (NO fire-function override — lowest engine risk):** combat reduces fire damage by dividing by `TERRAIN[tile.t].def`; the `.cover` field was defined but UNUSED. The module MUTATES the frozen consts `TERRAIN`/`TCOL`/`PALETTE` at load (adding keys to a const object is legal) to install the 6 cover types with real `def` values + period colors, so combat applies them automatically through the existing `.def` path. def ladder: stonewall 2.00 > trench 1.95 > sunkenroad 1.85 > boulders 1.70 > forest 1.50 > woodfence 1.25 (between clear 1.00 and works/fort 2.10). A stone wall halves casualties (probe: 100→50).
- **Placement:** OVERRIDES `authoredMap` (verbatim base body + a `tcDecorateMap` pass; added to manifest overrides → 2× collision-gate). `_tcCoverFor` matches feature labels → cover: Sunken Road→sunkenroad, Marye's Heights/Stone Wall→stonewall, Devil's Den/Round Top→boulders, the woods/Wilderness→forest, redan/redoubt/lunette/salient/retrenchment→trench. 11 stamps across 6 of 10 authored maps. Positions already `fort` (def 2.10) — the Vicksburg redans, Antietam's Bloody Lane — are correctly LEFT by the no-weaken guard. Procedural `genMap` battles aren't decorated (already carry woods/town/works cover).
- **Content:** 1 Verified teaching card (cover as graded killing ground — Fredericksburg's stone wall & sunken road; Hess / NPS-ABT / Griffith, the A2-vetted sources).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × independent verify, 13 agents) → 2 confirmed findings (both medium; the const-mutation timing + idempotency were probed and confirmed SAFE by the refuted set), both fixed:
  - **D44.1** `"trench"` substring-matched "The Retrenchment" (an accidental hit stamping a road tile). Fixed: dropped bare `"trench"` → `"trenches"` + added explicit `"retrenchment"` (anchored intent — The Retrenchment is a genuine Franklin fieldwork, kept as cover).
  - **D44.2** stamping swaps `tile.t`, which the engine also reads for MOVEMENT cost — and one case (Marye's ridge→stonewall) made high ground CHEAPER to cross, contradicting the "def only" claim. Fixed: stonewall cost 1→2 (a wall is an obstacle) + a **no-speedup guard** (never stamp if `cover.cost < tile.cost`) so decoration never reduces traversal cost; reframed the docs as an honest terrain swap (def↑, cost never↓, never water, preserves objectives/elevation).
- **Verified:** probe-cover **8/8** (def ladder, render colors, label matching incl. a Dunker-Church negative, stamping across 6 maps, Antietam Sunken Road strong-cover, never-weaken, the terrain-swap invariant [11 stamps: 0 weaker def, 0 cheaper-to-cross], combat reduction); diag-classic Classic paints (no regression from the override); full no-regression suite green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈962KB.

## D45 — A4 WIRE THE ARMORY → THE BATTLEFIELD: the weapons you buy are what your brigades fire — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The small arms bought in The Armory (`C.armory.loadout`) become what the player's brigades actually carry and fire. New `src/59-armory-field.js`. Frozen-engine override (§8.2): `genForce`.
- **Mechanism:** a battle unit's firepower is decided entirely by `WEAPONS[u.weapon].pow` (resolveFire ~1037). The module OVERRIDES `genForce` (verbatim base body + a re-arm pass) so a fraction of the PLAYER's fresh infantry are re-armed from the loadout, mapped armory-id → engine WEAPONS key (`smoothbore`→smooth … `henry`→henry, quality-MONOTONIC so a better buy is never a worse field weapon). Buy Spencers → a slice of the line carries "spencer" (pow 2.05 vs the musket's 1.00 = +105% fire). The remainder keeps standard issue; veterans keep their earned weapon; the enemy is untouched (no arsenal to draw on).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × independent verify, 16 agents) → 5 confirmed findings (the override fidelity confirmed byte-identical by the refuted set), all fixed:
  - **D45.1 (HIGH — Classic regression)** the re-arm fired whenever `G.campaign` merely existed (gated on `G.campaign.side`), so a **Free Battle with a saved campaign in memory could re-arm the AI ENEMY with the player's arsenal** (or silently self-buff a same-side free-battle force) — breaking Classic/Free-Battle independence from campaign state. Fixed: gate on `campaignCore` (the engine passes it non-null ONLY for the player force in a real `fromCampaign` battle; the enemy force and BOTH Free-Battle forces get null) — the exact discriminator.
  - **D45.2 (MED)** engine-era bypass: the armory's `data/weapons.json` year-gates are looser than the engine's `WEAPONS.era`, so the player could field e.g. Sharps at an 1861 battle the era-locked AI couldn't. Fixed: skip any weapon whose `WEAPONS.era` > the battle year (the bought arm fields only once the engine would issue it — fair vs the AI, no anachronism).
  - **D45.3 (LOW)** float drift: 0.1×10 = 0.9999… → `floor` left one brigade un-armed on a "100%-armed" line. Fixed: snap `fr>0.9995→1` + an epsilon on the floor.
- **Verified:** probe-armory-field **9/9** (monotonic mapping, player-not-enemy re-arm, fraction lower-bound, whole-army float-safe, veterans keep their weapon, Spencer +105% pow, off-campaign no-op, the engine-era gate [1861 Sharps→0 fielded], Free-Battle isolation [`{spencer:1.0}` live but core=null → not all armed = no leak]); diag-classic Classic paints (no regression from the `genForce` override); full no-regression suite green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈970KB.

## D46 — A5 TARGETING: VERIFIED the player already picks specific fire targets — NO engine change — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The backlog asked to "verify the player can pick specific targets + expose/polish it." Investigation + an empirical probe confirm the frozen engine ALREADY supports full player target choice, so A5 ships as a **verification**, not new code.
- **Mechanism (already in the engine):** `fireTargets(u)` (base ~1003) returns every alive, in-range, visible enemy hex; `onHexClick` (base ~1273) fires at the EXACT clicked hex (`resolveFire(sel,c,r)`) when in fire mode — the PLAYER chooses the target, not an auto/best pick (only the AI uses `chooseBestFireTarget`). Valid targets are highlighted (red circle + crosshair, both 2D Classic and 3D); full keyboard aiming (F → arrows → Enter).
- **Verified (probe-targeting 5/5):** two enemies placed in a player unit's weapon range → `fireTargets` returns BOTH (a real choice); entering fire mode populates/highlights `G.fireT`; clicking ONE specific enemy damages THAT enemy (512→483, 29 cas) and NOT the other (no auto-target leak); the firing unit is marked fired; an already-fired unit offers no targets (ammo/turn discipline). 0 pageerrors; the probe doubles as a post-A1–A4 battle smoke test (boot → select → fire → resolve all work).
- **Decision (decide-&-log):** ship NO engine change. The feature is complete and correct; bolting redundant targeting UI onto a working frozen engine would be over-engineering (§27) and needless §8.2 override risk. Optional future polish (a louder target highlight / hover "click to fire" tooltip) is deferred — not worth the risk now. No adversarial bug-hunt run (no new game code to attack; the empirical probe is the verification). Deliverable unchanged; only `tools/probe-targeting.mjs` added.

## D47 — A6a BATTLE-DAY CONDITIONING: the strategic war shapes the army that takes the field — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The bridge already COMPUTES the conditioned army (`bridgeArmy`) + prep; A6a APPLIES it. New `src/86-battle-conditioning.js` overrides `startBattleRuntime` (frozen-engine §8.2; verbatim base body + a `_a6Condition()` pass after `G.battle` is built). Campaign battles only (`B.fromCampaign`) — Free Battle / Classic / diag-classic untouched.
- **What it does:** scales the player force by `bridgeArmy(C)` — strength ×[0.88..1.12], morale +(facet−60)×0.3 — and applies `C.battlePrep` (entrench → +2 ent; forcedMarch → −6 morale; raidSupply → enemy −6 morale & −20% ammo). Field Fortifications (A2) → trench cover on ~25%·level of the line when the entrench order is given (the A2→A3→battlefield tie, end-to-end).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × independent verify, 15 agents) → 4 confirmed findings (the override confirmed byte-faithful by the refuted set), all fixed:
  - **D47.1 (§27 calibration — the key one)** a fresh campaign's `bridgeArmy.overall` is ~74-76, NOT 50, so anchoring `strengthMul` at 50=1.0 silently buffed every no-investment army ~+10% vs the frozen enemy. Re-anchored at 74 → a fresh army plays ≈ Classic (probe ratio **1.009**); a well-run war earns up to +12%, a failing one −12%.
  - **D47.2 (§27 over-stack)** narrowed the strength band ±20%→±12%, and **gated the auto-trench on the entrench prep order** (a deliberate slot, not a free always-on stack) so the tactical fight still decides at the extremes.
  - **D47.3 (feature gap)** the Field-Fortifications→trench tie was inert on the ~29/40 procedural-map battles (no `M.deploy`); now falls back to the player's own occupied hexes (the line they dig in on).
  - **D47.4** entrenching no longer re-terrains objective tiles (skip `t.obj`; preserve authored terrain).
- **Verified:** probe-conditioning **6/6** (strong>weak in-band; free-battle untouched; entrench +2 ent; raid-supply saps enemy morale; **fresh ≈ Classic, ratio 1.009**; fortifications trench gated on entrench — 68/91 when ordered, 0 without); diag-classic Classic paints (no regression from the `startBattleRuntime` override); full no-regression suite green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈977KB. **A6b — the bridge AUTO-RESOLVE (playable end-to-end) — is next.**

## D48 — A6b BRIDGE AUTO-RESOLVE: the owner-mode war is playable end-to-end — [CLAUDE] (run j, 2026-06-14)
The §8.19 keystone. New `src/87-auto-resolve.js` + an "Auto-resolve" button in the pre-battle briefing (`src/85`). Resolve a battle from the army your war fielded, without playing the tactical fight; "To the Field" (fight it) remains.
- **Mechanism:** `bridgeAutoResolve` builds the CONDITIONED battle (`startBattleRuntime` → A6a), `bridgeResolveOutcome` decides the result, then it drives the engine's OWN `campaignAdvance` — so an auto-resolved battle reconciles the roster, runs `_t1Resolve` (manpower/clock/strategy/enemyWill/victory), awards funds, and advances the chain IDENTICALLY to a fought one. Seeded RND → deterministic-by-performance (your strategy, not luck, decides it).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × independent verify, 24 agents) → 11 confirmed findings (deduped to 6 fixes; the `campaignAdvance` contract + no-field-flash confirmed sound by the refuted set), all fixed:
  - **D48.1 (HIGH — the big one)** the original margin compared the raw 0-100 `overall` ~1:1 vs the enemy, so a competent Union could NEVER lose and auto-resolve was strictly *easier than fighting* (a foregone-conclusion click-through). Re-anchored on the EDGE OVER BASELINE (me−74 vs foe−64 — the same anchors A6a / `_arEnemyRating` use), so a baseline army is a real gamble (losable like Classic) and auto-resolve is outcome-equivalent to fighting. Verified: strong war wins (margin 11), weak war loses (margin −28) — real jeopardy restored.
  - **D48.2 (HIGH — audio)** auto-resolve bypassed `endBattle`, so the battle music/wind bed played over the result/interstitial. Now calls `_audLeaveBattle()` + sets `G.mode="result"` + a win/loss bugle, matching `endBattle`.
  - **D48.3 (MED)** honors `C.flipAtk` (recovery role-flip) exactly as `launchCampaignBattle` — a recovery battle resolves in the correct defend orientation.
  - **D48.4 (MED)** XP parity — a win credits surviving regiments by magnitude (decisive → kills 2 → the +2 XP a decisive win deserves; normal → +1), matching the fought path.
  - **D48.5 (LOW)** symmetric casualty clamps + a winner-shatters-loser floor (decisive 72% / win 42%) so funds / `stats.infl` / enemyWill-erosion rewards match fighting (enemy bleeds ~40% on a win).
  - **D48.6** removed dead `_arSideStrength`.
- **Verified:** probe-auto-resolve **7/7** (strong out-resolves weak WITH jeopardy; both bleed, loser more; kill attribution; flipAtk honored; enemy-rating asymmetry CS 61→45 / US 55→63; `campaignAdvance` advances the war + feeds the tick; briefing offers Auto-resolve + Fight); diag-classic Classic paints; full no-regression green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈987KB.
- **⚑ THE BATTLE LAYER (A1–A6) IS COMPLETE — the owner-mode war is now PLAYABLE END-TO-END:** run the strategic desk → field a conditioned army (manpower/production/blockade/arms/cannon/engineers/morale) → at each battle auto-resolve or fight → the result feeds manpower/clock/strategy/victory → win via the chain or a path-to-victory. **NEXT: the strategic arc S2–S5** (cabinet/advisors, 3-layer morale, 1864 election, press, command/generals, emancipation, civil liberties, events).

## D49 — S2 m1 THE CABINET & ADVISOR SYSTEM (R25 linchpin / §8.22 / §8.54) — [CLAUDE] (run k, 2026-06-14)
The first S2 sub-system: the full historical cabinet replaces the S0 4-secretary stub. New `data/cabinet.json` + `src/31-cabinet.js` (overrides `presRenderCabinet`/`presWireCabinet`; `cabInit`/`cabOnResolve` registered in `90-president-register.js`). The S0 cabinet research run-id was from a prior session (unrecoverable), so content was researched fresh.
- **What it does:** the FULL roster per side is DATE-AWARE — the current holder of each office is whoever historically held it at the strategic date, so the CHURN is mechanical (Davis's revolving War office Walker→Benjamin→Randolph→Seddon→Breckinridge; Benjamin's three-post rotation War→State; Chase out July 1864; Cameron→Stanton). Each of the 4 principal advisors (war/treasury/state/navy) gives a one-line **recommendation keyed to the war state** (`_cabReading`: inflationHigh / armyWeak / recognitionRisk / blockadeLoose / always), a one-click **Heed** or **Delegate**, an expandable **why** (reasoning + teaching + provenance), and an **ambition tell** that surfaces for self-servers (high-ambition men always; moderate when their domain struggles). Plus a full-roster expander (the churn made legible) and the two cross-cutting teaching cards. Secondary offices (justice/post/interior) are roster/teaching-only.
- **Content:** the `s2-cabinet-research` workflow (21 agents, **web-grounded** + 2-pass adversarial verify) → 18 principal profiles + cross-cards, merged conservatively into `cabinet.json` (structure/tenures/condition-vocabulary preserved; voice/ambition/ambitionTell/stance-prose/cards grafted) then entity-normalized (decode HTML entities in the data so the render layer escapes exactly once — `&amp;`→`&`). Verified, multi-voice (4–7 perspectives/card), anti-Lost-Cause: Benjamin's antisemitic scapegoating, Memminger's structural finance failure ("why the South could not pay for its war"), Davis's micromanagement & states'-rights paralysis as real causes of defeat, the Union team-of-rivals that out-governed Richmond.
- **Mechanics (designer calibration, logged per §8.7):** Heed = a bounded once-per-turn nudge — base **+1 political capital at most once per strategic turn TOTAL** (D49.5 fix) + a per-domain micro-effect (treasury weariness −2 / war supply +2 / state intervention ±2 toward the side's interest / navy: CS importFactor +0.02 capped 1.1, US supply +1). Delegate = the auto-manage flag (flavor in m1; domain systems read it later). Ambition thresholds: ≥75 always-active, 45–74 active-when-domain-bad, <45 never. `cabinetLeadership(C)` (a 0–100 competence index from the sitting War/Navy secretaries, anchored 64) is **exposed but NOT yet consumed by `bridgeArmy`** — wiring + tuning deferred to the generals/command milestone (m5) where leadership is the headline; m1 is therefore a purely additive UI/teaching milestone with **zero battle-balance change** (D49.7 confirmed this by grep).
- **Decide-&-log:** (a) the cabinet Delegate and the per-system delegates (econ treasury) are independent surfaces in m1 — unifying them is later polish. (b) G.W. Smith's ~3-day acting War tenure is omitted from the holder roster (mentioned in card text) to keep date-selection clean. (c) per the owner's directive, **WebSearch/WebFetch grounding is now folded into the content workflows** (this one already was), strengthening the ≥2-source Verified bar.
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × 3-skeptic independent verify, **62 agents**) → **8 confirmed of 19 raw (11 refuted)**, all fixed:
  - **D49.1 (HIGH — save integrity)** a corrupt/imported save with `president` (or `P.date`) as a non-object primitive throws a strict-mode TypeError in `presInit` (assigning a property to a primitive), aborting the cabinet render. Fixed: `presInit` now coerces a primitive `president` to null (rebuild) and guards `date`/`head`/`cabinet`/`pendingChoices`/`log` against non-object/array shapes; `presRenderCabinet` wraps its init calls in try/catch (defense-in-depth).
  - **D49.2 (MED — silent dead UI)** a `cabinetState` persisted as an ARRAY passed the bare object check, so the per-domain keys cabInit added were dropped on the next JSON round-trip → Heed/Delegate became permanent no-ops. Fixed: `Array.isArray` rejection (matches the artInit/engInit idiom).
  - **D49.3 (MED — teaching accuracy)** `cabOnResolve` named the predecessor from the STALE domain snapshot, so a date that leaps across >1 tenure in one tick (the clock.year sync can jump a year) named the wrong predecessor and skipped offices. Fixed: new `_cabPrevHolder` names the tenure-immediate predecessor.
  - **D49.4 (LOW — content)** the CS Attorney-General had a Nov–Dec 1863 tenure gap; the no-window fallback resurrected Bragg (gone ~20 months) as "in office." Fixed in data: Watts's end extended 1863-10 → 1864-01 to abut George Davis.
  - **D49.5 (HIGH — balance)** cross-domain Heed stacking added +1 capital PER domain PER turn (up to +64 over the war), and capital feeds the 1864 reelection referendum — the engagement nudge could decide reelection over battle outcomes. Fixed: capital gated to **once per turn total** (`P.heedCapTurn`); domain micro-effects unchanged.
  - **D49.6 (LOW — consistency)** navy Heed was pure free capital; gave it a bounded side-appropriate micro-effect (above).
  - **D49.7 (LOW — scope confirm, NOT a bug)** `cabinetLeadership` confirmed not consumed by `bridgeArmy` → zero battle-balance change this milestone (validates the deferral). The exact m5 wiring is recorded.
  - **D49.8 (LOW — latent XSS hardening)** the President's-log render was unescaped `innerHTML`, and the cabinet now writes dynamic dispatch text into it; escaped both render sites with `_cabEsc` (trusted data today, defense-in-depth).
- **Verified:** probe-cabinet **12/12** (incl. 3 new steps locking D49.1/.2/.3/.5); full no-regression green (diag-classic Classic paints; desk 12/12 — updated to the new advisor UX; conditioning/auto-resolve/bridge/economy/victory/blockade/manpower/weapons/production/cannon/engineering/cover/armory-field/targeting unaffected); 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈1130KB. **NEXT: S2 m2 — curated decision cards + the `president.pendingChoices` loop (emancipation as a dated decision + civil-liberties dilemmas), `data/decisions.json`.**

## D50 — S2 m2 CURATED EXECUTIVE DECISIONS + the pendingChoices loop (§8.27 emancipation-dated · §8.62 civil liberties · §8.68 cadence) — [CLAUDE] (run k, 2026-06-14)
The S0 `president.pendingChoices` STUB becomes a real, non-blocking decision system. New `data/decisions.json` (an 8-card deck) + `src/32-decisions.js` (the engine). Decisions surface in the between-battles interstitial AND a new **"Decisions" desk tab** (the 11th); each card presents a real choice with honest bounded effects + teaching, or is left for later.
- **What it does:** `decOnResolve` (registered after pres/cab) OWNS the queue — adds eligible cards by trigger at the **§8.68 cadence (≤2 new non-hinge per turn; the hinge always surfaces)**, drops resolved/expired (re-validated through `_decEligible`). `presOnResolve` no longer clears `pendingChoices` (the S0 reset removed; decisions persist until answered). `decResolve` applies each option's bounded, clamped, LOGGED effects (the numbers live in the data; the applier maps field→game state: weariness/capital/intervention/importFactor/strength). The marquee card is **EMANCIPATION** — a dated Union HINGE (the war's sole hinge) with three real options (issue / go-radical-now / refuse), trading border-state loyalty (capital) against foreign opinion (intervention) and USCT manpower. It sets `C.president.emancipation`, which the **manpower module now reads to gate the USCT pool**: issue → unlocks (even pre-1863 if radical); refuse → never; **no decision → the historical 1863 calendar default holds (zero regression)**. Civil-liberties + home-front cards both sides: habeas corpus (US + CS), Vallandigham/Copperheads, the NYC draft riots, press censorship, the Richmond bread riot, the twenty-slave law.
- **Content:** the web-grounded `s2-decisions-research` workflow (17 agents, WebSearch/WebFetch + adversarial verify) → real public sources WITH URLs (National Archives Emancipation Proclamation, Library of Congress, the Freedmen & Southern Society Project, Dickinson's House Divided, the Greeley/Browning/Corning letters, Neely's *The Fate of Liberty*, McCurry's *Confederate Reckoning*, Foner, Oakes). Merged conservatively (the 3 scaffold cards' ids/option-ids/effects preserved so the probe + engine contract held; 5 new cards translated from qualitative tradeoffs into bounded effects), then entity-normalized. Anti-Lost-Cause + Black-agency-centered (Du Bois's general strike; the self-emancipating enslaved forcing the question; the twenty-slave law's "rich man's war").
- **Decide-&-log:** (a) **emancipation is the ONLY hinge** — the research merge marked 6 cards as hinges, which would surface 4+ at once and break the cadence; reset to emancipation-only so cadence stays "1–2/turn, more at the hinge." (b) the cabinet Delegate and decision queue are independent surfaces. (c) the USCT gate keeps the 1863 calendar as the default so old saves + a player who ignores the card behave exactly as before.
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × 3-skeptic verify, **56 agents**, 3.0M tokens) → **12 confirmed of 17 (5 refuted)**, all fixed:
  - **D50.1 (MED — cross-module save integrity)** `manpowerOnResolve` read `C.president.emancipation` RAW and ticks BEFORE `decOnResolve`, so a corrupt primitive emancipation could mis-drive the one-way USCT latch. Fixed: manpower calls `decInit(C)` first (sanitizes the field → treated as "no decision").
  - **D50.2 (LOW)** `decInit` de-dups `pendingChoices` (corrupt/double-push → duplicate cards with colliding DOM ids).
  - **D50.3 (LOW)** the resolved-history render skips non-string option ids (no "[object Object]").
  - **D50.4 (MED)** `decOnResolve`'s drop-filter delegates to `_decEligible`, so a corrupt cross-side/ineligible id is evicted on the next tick.
  - **D50.5 (LOW)** probe-decisions enforces card-id uniqueness at the gate.
  - **D50.6 / D50.7 (HIGH)** `decResolve` had NO idempotency guard — a card could be re-resolved, re-applying effects and flipping emancipation issue↔decline AFTER the manpower gate irreversibly banked the USCT pool. Fixed: resolved cards are TERMINAL + only a currently-pending card can be resolved.
  - **D50.8 (HIGH — balance)** the applier upper-clamped capital at 100, but the frozen clock treats capital as unbounded-above (and the 1864 referendum reads it) → decisions silently DESTROYED capital above 100. Fixed: capital is floor-only (`Math.max(0, …)`), matching the clock.
  - **D50.9 (LOW)** Array guards on `c.options` (malformed deck degrades, no throw).
  - **D50.10 (LOW)** the strength applier floor aligned to the manpower module's own floor of 5.
  - **D50.11 (LOW)** card/option ids sanitized (`_decIdSafe`) identically on the render-attribute and `getElementById`-selector sides (defensive).
  - **D50.12 (scope confirm — NOT a bug)** decisions are strictly campaign-gated; cannot perturb Classic / Free Battle. Added a save-round-trip + null-field probe step.
- **Verified:** probe-decisions **14/14**; probe-desk **13/13** (incl. the new Decisions tab); probe-manpower **9/9** (the USCT-gate edit no-regression); diag-classic Classic paints; full no-regression green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈1237KB. **NEXT: S2 m3 — 3-layer morale (troop/leader/public-will-decides-late) wired to the 1864 election hinge.**

## D51 — S2 m3 THE THREE-LAYER MORALE SYSTEM + the 1864 election hinge (§8.61/D39.2 · §8.67/D41.2) — [CLAUDE] (run k, 2026-06-14)
Three interacting, visible morale layers + the home-front-decides-the-war wiring. New `src/33-morale.js` + `C.morale`; surfaced as a **"The Nation's Will"** block in the War Effort overview.
- **What it does:** `moraleCompute(C)` derives three layers fresh each turn from the war state, with the INTERACTIONS in the formulas: **TROOP** morale (battle conditioning via `bridgeArmy.morale` + supply, **lifted by leadership**); **LEADER** reputation (win-rate + the sitting cabinet's `cabinetLeadership`, dragged down by an active ambition tell); **PUBLIC** will (**sunk by the accumulating casualty toll** [D35.6 human-cost] **and runaway inflation**, lifted by victories + the South's hope of recognition, modulated by leadership). The block also shows a **1864-election forecast** mirroring the frozen clock's own support formula.
- **The 1864 election → strategic outcome (D41.2):** the frozen `clkOnResolve` already resolves the referendum from `100 − weariness + capital/2 + winRate·20` (weariness IS the public-will proxy). m3 adds the CONSEQUENCE in `moraleOnResolve` (runs AFTER clk, BEFORE vic): when the verdict lands (once, `electionApplied` latch), it feeds the EXISTING `C.strategy.enemyWill` — **re-elected → enemyWill −8** (a determined administration grinds the enemy down toward your negotiated-peace win); **repudiated → enemyWill +12 + a public-will hit** (the home front broke; the enemy takes heart). So you can win every battle and still lose the war if the public will fails — and the ballot box is the South's surest road to a negotiated peace (§8.52).
- **Decide-&-log:** (a) **morale is a computed READOUT with exactly ONE sim coupling** (the bounded one-time election→enemyWill nudge) — it writes NOTHING to the frozen clock/economy/manpower, so it cannot regress their assertions; the 3 layers are derived, not accumulated (no feedback loop). (b) The election coupling feeds the EXISTING victory module (enemyWill→victoryReady, D26) rather than a new path; full victory/defeat *resolution* (incl. a US-side election-loss ending) remains S5's job. (c) The casualty toll is a SEPARATE accumulator from the clock's per-battle weariness (intended — the toll is the cumulative human cost that sinks public will over the whole war). (d) `morale.troop` mirrors the battle-side morale the bridge already uses; wiring morale BACK into the bridge is deferred (battle-balance protected this milestone).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × 3-skeptic verify, **29 agents**) → **7 confirmed of 8 (1 refuted — it validated that morale writes nothing to the frozen clock/economy/manpower)**, all fixed:
  - **D51.1 (HIGH — save migration)** the one-time election→enemyWill latch (`electionApplied`) was presence-checked, so a legacy/pre-morale save already past the 1864 verdict (`resolved1864` true, no `C.morale`) would RE-FIRE the enemyWill nudge on load. Fixed: `moraleInit` seeds `electionApplied = !!(clk.resolved1864)` (a verdict already resolved at init = already applied) — migration-safe, no `_SAVE_VER` bump (the D7 pattern).
  - **D51.3 / D51.5 (HIGH/MED)** the latch was burned BEFORE the effect landed, so a turn with `C.strategy` absent would seal it and lose the consequence forever. Fixed: the latch is now set ATOMICALLY inside the `S && enemyWill` guard (mirrors D49.5) — it only seals when the nudge applies, and retries next turn otherwise.
  - **D51.2 (MED)** a corrupt negative `casualtyToll` inverted the casualty penalty and pinned public will to 100. Fixed: `moraleInit` floors the toll to ≥0 (`!(x>=0)` also catches NaN/−Infinity); `casPenalty` lower-bounded `Math.max(0, …)`.
  - **D51.4 (MED/LOW)** the repudiation `M.public −= 10` was an inert one-tick write (public is recomputed each tick, clobbering it). Fixed: replaced with a DURABLE `M.repudiated` flag that `moraleCompute` reads (a persistent −12 public-will penalty) — the "home front breaks" now actually shows and lasts.
  - **D51.6 (refuted → NONE)** the integration lens confirmed morale writes ONLY `C.morale` + the one bounded enemyWill nudge (no frozen-clock/economy/manpower writes; `moraleCompute` only READS `bridgeArmy`/`cabinetLeadership` — no recursion), so the no-regression guarantee holds by construction.
- **Verified:** probe-morale **10/10** (the 3 layers + interactions, casualty/inflation sinks, leadership-lifts-troops, toll accumulation, the 1864 election→enemyWill in both directions, render, AND the D51.1/.2/.3 corrupt/legacy-save hardening); full no-regression green (probe-victory **12/12**, blockade/manpower/bridge/auto-resolve/desk/economy/decisions/cabinet/conditioning/weapons/production/cannon/engineering/cover/armory-field/targeting all green; diag-classic Classic paints); 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈1249KB. **NEXT: S2 m4 — the press / public-opinion system (§8.57/D38.1): period papers react to your war → public morale + the 1864 election; censorship/Vallandigham as a lever; ties the broadsheet UI to the 3-layer morale.**

## D52 — S2 m4 THE PRESS / PUBLIC-OPINION SYSTEM (§8.57 / D38.1) — [CLAUDE] (run k, 2026-06-14)
The real Civil War newspapers, North and South, react to your war with period broadsheet editorials — a real driver of the public will that decides the 1864 election. New `data/press.json` (12 papers) + `src/34-press.js` + `C.press`; surfaced as a new **"The Press"** desk tab (the 12th, period broadsheet).
- **What it does:** each paper has a real political LEAN (radical / administration / war-democrat / copperhead / fire-eater / abolitionist) that sets HOW it reacts. `pressOnResolve` (runs BEFORE `moraleOnResolve`) reads the turn's condition (victory / defeat / stalemate / heavy-casualties / emancipation-once), each paper runs a matching editorial and shifts its FAVOR toward/against the war effort (strongly-for +8 … strongly-against −8, clamped 0-100; a paper with no editorial for today's news drifts back toward its standing lean), and the aggregate SENTIMENT feeds `moraleCompute`'s public-will layer (`pressTerm = (sentiment−50)·0.2`, ±10) — so the press is a real driver of the home front. The tab shows the day's headlines, each paper's stance, and the aggregate.
- **Content:** the web-grounded `s2-press-research` workflow (7 agents, WebSearch/WebFetch + adversarial verify) → 12 real papers with real editors + URLs (Greeley's *Tribune*, Garrison's *Liberator*, Medill's *Chicago Tribune*, Curtis's *Harper's Weekly*; the *NY World*, *Chicago Times*, *Crisis*, *Herald* Copperhead/Democratic sheets; the *Richmond Examiner* & *Charleston Mercury* savaging Davis, the *Enquirer* defending him, the *Dispatch*). Merged conservatively (the 4 scaffold ids/leans preserved). Anti-Lost-Cause throughline: BOTH presses were bitterly divided — the Confederate press was no propaganda monolith but raged at Davis, conscription, and impressment; the *Herald*'s ahistorical "war-independent" lean was mapped to the contract's `war-democrat`.
- **Decide-&-log:** (a) the press is a READOUT + ONE read-only coupling (morale reads `pressSentiment`) — it writes nothing to the frozen clock/economy/manpower/strategy (zero regression); `pressSentiment` is a NEUTRAL 50 until the press first reacts, so it perturbs nothing at init / in the morale probe. (b) the cross-cutting teaching cards intentionally name papers from BOTH sides (a press-landscape lesson) — they are NOT side-filtered; only the player's PAPER LIST is side-scoped. (c) the censorship/Vallandigham LEVER is the existing m2 decision cards (`us-press-censorship`/`us-vallandigham`) acting on public opinion; a deeper standing-censorship tie to per-paper favor is a future deepening.
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (5 lenses × 3-skeptic verify, **44 agents**) → **7 confirmed of 13 (6 refuted)**, all fixed:
  - **D52.1 (MED — save integrity)** `pressInit` repaired only the array-ness of `C.press.headlines`, not the entries, so a corrupt/legacy save with a `null` headline entry crashed `pressRenderTab` → froze the whole Press tab (the `_wdRefresh` dispatch isn't wrapped). Fixed: `pressInit` filters headlines to well-formed objects + a `!hd` continue-guard in the render.
  - **D52.2 / D52.6 (LOW)** the sentiment guards were NaN-blind (`typeof NaN === "number"`). Fixed: `pressInit` + `pressSentiment` reject non-finite / out-of-range sentiment (so a corrupt NaN can't poison `moraleCompute`'s public will).
  - **D52.3 (LOW — calibration)** the heavy-casualties priority ran over a victory's rally, but the heavy-casualties editorials were `neutral` → a bloody win read as a no-op. Fixed in data: the "mournful column" → `against` (a bloody victory now visibly TEMPERS the press — historically faithful to the bloody 1864 victories that sapped Northern morale); the abolitionist "blood atones" stays neutral (its distinctive framing).
  - **D52.4 (LOW)** the emancipation-once latch was set whenever the condition was active even if no paper actually printed an emancipation editorial. Fixed: the latch is set ONLY when a paper ran an emancipation editorial (`firedEmancipation`).
  - **D52.5 (LOW)** `_prsConditions` trusted the caller's `"draw"` string for stalemate; now also treats `winnerSide == null` as a stalemate (mirrors `endBattle`).
  - **D52.7 (LOW)** an editorial with an empty headline could push an empty broadsheet line; gated on `ed.headline`.
- **Verified:** probe-press **10/10** (papers load side-correct, neutral-until-reacted, victory>defeat sentiment, the Copperhead turns on a defeat, emancipation-splits-once latch, the press→public-will coupling anchored at 50, CS paper-list correctness, render, AND the D52.1/.2/.4 hardening + the bloody-day dampener); probe-desk **13/13** (the new Press tab); probe-morale **10/10** (the `pressTerm` edit anchored = no change); full no-regression green; 0 pageerrors. Deliverable ≈1300KB.
- **Tooling note:** running TWO browser-probe batteries concurrently collides on the shared `:8765` server + `tools/shots/*.json` → ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED / goto-timeout flakes + cross-overwritten result files. **Run probe batteries SEQUENTIALLY, one battery at a time.**

## D53 — S2 m5 COMMAND: the NAMED-GENERALS system + the bridge LEADERSHIP wiring (§8.24/§8.58 · D31.4/D38.2 · GRAND-STRATEGY §19) — [CLAUDE] (run k, 2026-06-14)
The LAST big S2 sub-system: the President appoints / promotes / relieves the commanding general of his principal army, and the sitting general (skill + evolving reputation) blended with the cabinet finally drives the **bridge LEADERSHIP facet** that was a `var leadership = 64;` placeholder since the battle layer (D49.7). New `data/generals.json` (20 generals) + `src/35-command.js` + `C.president.command`; a new **"Command"** desk tab (the 13th).
- **What it does:** each historical commander carries traits (**skill / aggression / caution**), an **evolving reputation** (rises with victory, falls with defeat — `cmdOnResolve`), and **ambition** (the McClellan problem). A **date-aware DEFAULT** holds the post if the player never intervenes (`_cmdHistoricalDefault`, the `_cabHolder` idiom): the single-slot **iconic-army chain** — US Army of the Potomac → general-in-chief (Scott → McClellan → Burnside → Hooker → Meade → Grant), CS Army of Northern Virginia (J.E. Johnston → Lee). Appointing a specific general LOCKS the post; **relieving costs political capital** (`clock.capital`), gated for a `very-costly` (popular, politically dangerous) general — the McClellan dilemma made mechanical, with a free "restore the historical command" escape valve.
- **THE KEY WIRING (the milestone's point):** `commandLeadership(C) = clamp(42,88, 64 + (genRating−64)·0.7 + (cabinetLeadership−64)·0.3)`, `genRating = 0.55·skill + 0.45·reputation`. **Anchored at 64** — a neutral general + neutral cabinet = 64 = the old constant, so a fresh/default command is byte-equivalent to Classic (the A6a/D47.1 anchor lesson). `src/85` line 90 now consumes it, and `bridgeArmy.overall` gains a **bidirectional leadership edge** `+(leadership−64)·0.18` (mirrors the additive artillery/engineering arms, but signed) — a masterful command lifts the army a few points, a poor/discredited one drags it; at the anchor the edge is exactly 0. The general's temperament also nudges the **auto-resolve margin** (`commandMarginEdge`: aggressive presses the attack, cautious is sound on defense; deterministic, ±~2). Reputation evolution (win +3 / decisive +6 / loss −4 / decisive −8 / draw −1, clamped 5–98) means a defeated commander's army weakens while a victor's separation widens.
- **Content:** the web-grounded `s2-generals-research` workflow (10 agents: 4 research clusters + 4 adversarial-verify + cross-roster balance + teaching cards; WebSearch/WebFetch) → 20 generals (US 10 / CS 10) + 4 multi-voice teaching cards (the McClellan problem; the Lost Cause & the generals; "Grant the butcher" rebutted; what makes a general). **Anti-Lost-Cause throughout:** Lee excellent-not-infallible (Gettysburg/Pickett's Charge); Grant/Sherman/Thomas top-tier; Forrest's bio NAMES Fort Pillow + the KKK + slave-trading; Bragg/Hood poor army commanders.
- **Decide-&-log:** (a) **single-slot default = the iconic army** (the bridge fields one army; the West/secondary commanders — Thomas, Sherman, Sheridan, Halleck, A.S. Johnston, Beauregard, Bragg, Hood — are fully APPOINTABLE via `availableFrom` but `commandFrom`-null so they don't hijack the default chain or jump theaters). (b) **the general is confined to the BRIDGE + auto-resolve, NOT the m3 morale leader layer** — `33-morale.js` deliberately keeps `cabinetLeadership` (NOT `commandLeadership`): routing the general in would double-count the cabinet (commandLeadership already folds it in) AND confound the cabinet-isolating morale probe (which varies the DATE to vary the cabinet, also varying the date-derived default general). Folding the general into morale is deferred. (c) **anchored zero-regression** — every battle-layer + morale assertion holds (verified empirically below).
- **Adversarial bug-hunt** (8 dimensions × independent skeptic verify, **20 agents**) → **9 confirmed of 12, all fixed:**
  - **D53.1 (HIGH — data) Thomas wrongly defaulted the US chain.** Thomas commanded the Army of the *Cumberland* (West), but his `commandFrom` (1863-10, later than Meade's 1863-06) made `_cmdHistoricalDefault` pick him over Meade Oct 1863–Mar 1864. Fixed: `commandFrom/commandTo → null` (appointable, not default). My first chain-probe missed it (didn't sample 1863-10→1864-03).
  - **D53.2 (MED — data) Sherman same.** His `commandFrom` (1864-03, the Military Division of the Mississippi) tied Grant's; nulled (appointable). US chain is now bulletproof: …Meade → Grant.
  - **D53.4 (HIGH — recursion landmine) `bridgeArmy → commandLeadership → cabinetLeadership → _cabAmbitionActive → _cabReading("war") → bridgeArmy`.** m5 closed a cycle that would stack-overflow whenever the sitting War Secretary has `ambitionTell` + ambition in [45,75). Dormant under current data (probes were green) but a data-change crash. Fixed: a re-entrancy guard `_brgLeadGuard` in `bridgeArmy` — a nested call uses the neutral 64 anchor, the outer call gets the true value. (Chose the guard over the verifier's "_cabReading uses manpower.strength" so the cabinet's war-reading heuristic + its probe stay intact.)
  - **D53.5 (HIGH — edge) post-war fallback jumped to the FIRST commander.** `_cmdHistoricalDefault`'s no-window fallback returned the earliest `commandFrom` (Scott) when a campaign ran past the last tenure end. Fixed: before the first tenure → earliest; after the last → the LATEST-ending commander (continuity).
  - **D53.6 (MED — save) `_activeId` rode the save unvalidated.** The handover-detection cache could reference a removed/wrong-side general after a roster change. Fixed: `cmdInit` clears it if not in the side roster (a just-died-but-in-roster id is KEPT so the succession still logs).
  - **D53.7 (MED — UX) capital soft-lock.** The pool rounded `clock.capital` for display but `cmdAppoint` gated on the raw value → a fractional capital could show an affordable button that silently failed. Fixed: round at the gate too.
  - **D53.8 (MED — XSS) `_cmdTraitBar(label,hint)` unescaped.** Call sites are hardcoded today, but the signature was injection-prone; now `_cmdEsc`'d (D43.4 discipline).
  - **D53.9 (MED — DOM) wire/render id-escape mismatch.** Render escaped the appoint-button id, `cmdWireTab` didn't; harmless for kebab ids but inconsistent. Now both `_cmdEsc`.
  - **D53.10 (LOW) dead inner ternary** in `_cmdGenRow` (the outer guard already proved `availableUntil` truthy). Simplified.
- **Verified:** probe-command **14/14** (data/schema, cmdInit + reputation seeding, the **fresh anchor 72→overall 77 Classic-safe**, date-aware default, appoint Grant lead 87 vs Burnside 52, reputation 88→98 win / 88→64 loss, the McClellan relief gate at 27 capital, the trait margin edge, the **D53-decoupling** [general moves the bridge, leaves the cabinet-driven leader layer], lock/revert, side-correctness, render, + the **D53.4 recursion guard** and **D53.5 post-war** regression guards); full no-regression GREEN — bridge 6/6 · conditioning 6/6 (the fresh-Classic anchor) · auto-resolve 7/7 · cabinet 12/12 · morale 10/10 · desk 13/13 · press/decisions/victory/manpower/economy/production/blockade/weapons/cannon/engineering/cover/targeting/armory-field/cab-exploit all green · diag-classic Classic paints; **0 pageerrors** throughout. Deliverable ≈1392KB. **S2 is COMPLETE (m1–m5). NEXT: S3 alt-history · S4 education/codex/tutorial/WCAG-AA · S5 victory + graded report + Reconstruction · then the run-k graphics/footage + survival/loot directives.**
